\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Velocity i at local node n. Uses suitably interpolated value for hanging nodes. The use of \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a7d8645f76ff2ef520a6c0e089272199d}{u\+\_\+index\+\_\+nst()}} permits the use of this element as the basis for multi-\/physics elements. \begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Return the index at which the i-\/th unknown velocity component is stored. The default value, i, is appropriate for single-\/physics problems. In derived multi-\/physics elements, this function should be overloaded to reflect the chosen storage scheme. Note that these equations require that the unknowns are always stored at the same indices at each node. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a8df9a643850f89105b6ff58afc7d6030}{get\+\_\+traction}} (const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_ab7123126e4885ef647dd9c6e3807a21c}{s}}, const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&N, Vector$<$ double $>$ \&traction)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Compute traction (on the viscous scale) exerted onto the fluid at local coordinate s. N has to be outer unit normal to the fluid. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a4d36c0d4e4d67e7adcf7d95770fc5622}{get\+\_\+traction}} (const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_ab7123126e4885ef647dd9c6e3807a21c}{s}}, const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&N, Vector$<$ double $>$ \&traction\+\_\+p, Vector$<$ double $>$ \&traction\+\_\+visc\+\_\+n, Vector$<$ double $>$ \&traction\+\_\+visc\+\_\+t)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Compute traction (on the viscous scale) exerted onto the fluid at local coordinate s, decomposed into pressure and normal and tangential viscous components. N has to be outer unit normal to the fluid. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a233e1cd44c42ab6b9b868e98ac7190e6}{get\+\_\+load}} (const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&\mbox{\hyperlink{cfortran_8h_ab7123126e4885ef647dd9c6e3807a21c}{s}}, const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&N, Vector$<$ double $>$ \&load)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em This implements a pure virtual function defined in the FSIFluid\+Element class. The function computes the traction (on the viscous scale), at the element\textquotesingle{}s local coordinate s, that the fluid element exerts onto an adjacent solid element. The number of arguments is imposed by the interface defined in the FSIFluid\+Element -- only the unit normal N (pointing into the fluid!) is actually used in the computation. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item 
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a3e99808dfc8f12ec389141796870d265}{get\+\_\+pressure\+\_\+and\+\_\+velocity\+\_\+mass\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+diagonal}} (Vector$<$ double $>$ \&press\+\_\+mass\+\_\+diag, Vector$<$ double $>$ \&veloc\+\_\+mass\+\_\+diag, const unsigned \&which\+\_\+one=0)
\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em Compute the diagonal of the velocity/pressure mass matrices. If which one=0, both are computed, otherwise only the pressure (which\+\_\+one=1) or the velocity mass matrix (which\+\_\+one=2 -- the LSC version of the preconditioner only needs that one) \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\begin{DoxyCompactList}\small\item\em This implements a pure virtual function defined in the FSIFluid\+Element class. The function computes the traction (on the viscous scale), at the element\textquotesingle{}s local coordinate s, that the fluid element exerts onto an adjacent solid element. The number of arguments is imposed by the interface defined in the FSIFluid\+Element -- only the unit normal N (pointing into the fluid!) is actually used in the computation. \end{DoxyCompactList}\item

\DoxyHorRuler{0}
 \hypertarget{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_autotoc_md23}{}\doxysubsubsection{SPACE-\/\+TIME ELEMENTS\+:}\label{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_autotoc_md23}
The space-\/time extension is written ONLY for the 2D Navier-\/\+Stokes equations. The result is a 3D problem (x,y,t) to be solved on a 3D mesh. The template parameter DIM now corresponds to the dimension of the space-\/time problem (i.\+e. DIM=3 for the 2D flow).

$ { \frac{\partial u_i}{\partial x_i}=Q } $

We also provide all functions required to use this element in FSI problems, by deriving it from the FSIFluid\+Element base class.

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_body\_force\_nst()}{get\_body\_force\_nst()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$unsigned DIM$>$ \\
virtual void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations}{Space\+Time\+Navier\+Stokes\+Equations}}$<$ DIM $>$\+::get\+\_\+body\+\_\+force\+\_\+nst (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const double \&}]{time,  }\item[{const unsigned \&}]{ipt,  }\item[{const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{s,  }\item[{const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{x,  }\item[{Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{result }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}



Calculate the body force at a given time and local and/or Eulerian position. This function is virtual so that it can be overloaded in multi-\/physics elements where the body force might depend on another variable.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$unsigned DIM$>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations}{Space\+Time\+Navier\+Stokes\+Equations}}$<$ DIM $>$\+::get\+\_\+load (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{s,  }\item[{const Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{N,  }\item[{Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{load }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



This implements a pure virtual function defined in the FSIFluid\+Element class. The function computes the traction (on the viscous scale), at the element\textquotesingle{}s local coordinate s, that the fluid element exerts onto an adjacent solid element. The number of arguments is imposed by the interface defined in the FSIFluid\+Element -- only the unit normal N (pointing into the fluid!) is actually used in the computation.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$unsigned DIM$>$ \\
void \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations}{Space\+Time\+Navier\+Stokes\+Equations}}$<$ DIM $>$\+::get\+\_\+pressure\+\_\+and\+\_\+velocity\+\_\+mass\+\_\+matrix\+\_\+diagonal (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{press\+\_\+mass\+\_\+diag,  }\item[{Vector$<$ double $>$ \&}]{veloc\+\_\+mass\+\_\+diag,  }\item[{const unsigned \&}]{which\+\_\+one = {\ttfamily 0} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute the diagonal of the velocity/pressure mass matrices. If which one=0, both are computed, otherwise only the pressure (which\+\_\+one=1) or the velocity mass matrix (which\+\_\+one=2 -- the LSC version of the preconditioner only needs that one) 

Compute the diagonal of the velocity/pressure mass matrices. If which one=0, both are computed, otherwise only the pressure (which\+\_\+one=1) or the velocity mass matrix (which\+\_\+one=2 -- the LSC version of the preconditioner only needs that one).

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{kin\_energy()}{kin\_energy()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$unsigned DIM$>$ \\
double \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations}{Space\+Time\+Navier\+Stokes\+Equations}}$<$ DIM $>$\+::kin\+\_\+energy}



Get integral of kinetic energy over element. 

Get integral of kinetic energy over element\+: Note that this is the \char`\"{}raw\char`\"{} kinetic energy in the sense that the density ratio has not been included. In problems with two or more fluids the user will have to remember to premultiply certain elements by the appropriate density ratio.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$unsigned DIM$>$ \\
virtual unsigned \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations}{Space\+Time\+Navier\+Stokes\+Equations}}$<$ DIM $>$\+::u\+\_\+index\+\_\+nst (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const unsigned \&}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}



Return the index at which the i-\/th unknown velocity component is stored. The default value, i, is appropriate for single-\/physics problems. In derived multi-\/physics elements, this function should be overloaded to reflect the chosen storage scheme. Note that these equations require that the unknowns are always stored at the same indices at each node.

\mbox{\Hypertarget{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a70d0efc9cb622914656c96f332f304ad}\label{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a70d0efc9cb622914656c96f332f304ad}} 
\index{SpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations$<$ DIM $>$@{SpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations$<$ DIM $>$}!u\_nst@{u\_nst}}
\index{u\_nst@{u\_nst}!SpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations$<$ DIM $>$@{SpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations$<$ DIM $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{u\_nst()}{u\_nst()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/6]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$unsigned DIM$>$ \\
double \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations}{Space\+Time\+Navier\+Stokes\+Equations}}$<$ DIM $>$\+::u\+\_\+nst (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const unsigned \&}]{n,  }\item[{const unsigned \&}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}



Velocity i at local node n. Uses suitably interpolated value for hanging nodes. The use of \mbox{\hyperlink{classSpaceTimeNavierStokesEquations_a7d8645f76ff2ef520a6c0e089272199d}{u\+\_\+index\+\_\+nst()}} permits the use of this element as the basis for multi-\/physics elements. The default is to assume that the i-\/th velocity component is stored at the i-\/th location of the node.
